## CHAPTER THIRTEEN

# Single Herbs

<!-- chunk -->

## INSTRUCTIONS FOR PREPARING AND USING SINGLE HERBS

<!-- chunk -->

### his chapter provides you with instructions for preparing and using

<!-- chunk -->

### single herbs. We’ve included information about each plant’s energetics and

<!-- chunk -->

### properties as well as warnings. We’ve also listed which major bulk herb

<!-- chunk -->

### suppliers carry the herb. Directions for making preparations are starting

<!-- chunk -->

### suggestions; feel free to experiment.

# AÇAÍ

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Euterpe oleracea

<!-- chunk -->

### Like other berries, açaí berries are loaded with antioxidants that help to protect

<!-- chunk -->

### cells from damage that may lead to chronic diseases such as heart disease,

<!-- chunk -->

### diabetes, and cancer. Açaí berry contains vitamin A, fiber, calcium, iron,

<!-- chunk -->

### essential fatty acids (omega-9), anthocyanins (antioxidant), and polysterols. The

<!-- chunk -->

### Journal of Agricultural and Food Chemistry published a 2008 study showing

<!-- chunk -->

### that the açaí berry has more antioxidants than blackberries, blueberries,

<!-- chunk -->

### strawberries, and raspberries, but fewer antioxidants than red wine and

<!-- chunk -->

### pomegranate juice.


<!-- chunk -->

### Cooling and nourishing


<!-- chunk -->

### Anti-inflammatory, antioxidant, and nutritive


# FRESH OR DRIED BERRIES:

<!-- chunk -->

### A handful of the berries 2–3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### 1 500 mg capsule 1–2 times daily with food


<!-- chunk -->

### 1–5 grams 1–2 times daily with food

# JUICE:

<!-- chunk -->

### 1–4 ounces 1–2 times daily with food

# AGRIMONY

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Agrimonia eupatoria

<!-- chunk -->

### Agrimony is an astringent that helps stop urinary bleeding and diarrhea. It’s

<!-- chunk -->

### helpful for those with cloudy, smelly urine and for those with incontinence. It

<!-- chunk -->

### also has an energetic action on the nervous system and helps to relieve emotional

<!-- chunk -->

### tension. Its indication as a flower remedy is a good guide to its herbal use—it

<!-- chunk -->

### helps people who mask their pain behind a facade of cheerfulness. It’s helpful

<!-- chunk -->

### for people who have a tense pulse and appear friendly and cheerful, but are

<!-- chunk -->

### actually very tense and stressed. It is a great urinary tract remedy and helps

<!-- chunk -->

### urinary tract infections and cystitis. It also helps constricted liver chi, a pattern in

<!-- chunk -->

### traditional Chinese medicine that is commonly seen in many Americans. This

<!-- chunk -->

### involves an inner resistance, anger, or frustration that constricts blood flow to the

<!-- chunk -->

### liver and creates a tense, wiry pulse. Agrimony relaxes blood flow to the liver

<!-- chunk -->

### and helps a person relax and go with the flow of life.


<!-- chunk -->

### Drying and relaxing


<!-- chunk -->

### Rolla Thomas: Atonic conditions of the urinary apparatus,

<!-- chunk -->

### and where the urine is thick and gelatinous. Improves the tone of all mucous

<!-- chunk -->

### membranes.


<!-- chunk -->

### Anti-inflammatory, astringent, hemostatic, and vulnerary


<!-- chunk -->

### Fresh leaf (1:2, 95% alcohol); dried leaf (1:5, 50% alcohol); 5 drops


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried leaf (1:6); ¼–1 tsp. 3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### For skin rashes, apply the salve or ointment as needed, or prepare a

<!-- chunk -->

### compress from a strong infusion or a decoction and apply several times daily.

# ALFALFA

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Medicago sativa

<!-- chunk -->

### Alfalfa has been called the king of herbs, and it has been used since ancient

<!-- chunk -->

### times. Roots can grow 30–60 feet deep to pick up minerals and water other

<!-- chunk -->

### plants can’t reach. This makes alfalfa a rich source of vitamins, minerals, trace

<!-- chunk -->

### minerals, and other nutrients. Its trace mineral content is probably what makes it

<!-- chunk -->

### valuable for the pituitary, because trace mineral deficiencies often affect this

<!-- chunk -->

### gland. It acts as a mild alterative and blood purifier and has been used for

<!-- chunk -->

### arthritis, poor appetite, general weakness, and mineral deficiencies. Alfalfa and

<!-- chunk -->

### peppermint make a good tea for digestive troubles.


<!-- chunk -->

### Alfalfa contains canavanine, a nonprotein amino acid that induces

<!-- chunk -->

### lupus-like symptoms in monkeys. There are several reports of this in humans as

<!-- chunk -->

### well. It is contraindicated in those with lupus.


<!-- chunk -->

### Moistening and nourishing


<!-- chunk -->

### Anticoagulant (blood thinner), bitter, galactagogue, mineralizer,

<!-- chunk -->

### and nutritive


<!-- chunk -->

### Sprouts may be added to a variety of foods and eaten daily.

# SOUTHERN DECOCTION:

<!-- chunk -->

### 1 cup 1–2 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Alcohol is not a good solvent of minerals, so tinctures are rarely used.

# BULK POWDER, CAPSULES, AND TABLETS:

<!-- chunk -->

### 1,000–4,000 mg, 2–3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried leaf (1:6); 2–10 ml (0.4–2 tsp.) 3 times daily

# ALOE VERA

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Aloe vera, syn. A. barbadensis

<!-- chunk -->

### Aloe vera juice and gel are made from the inner pulp of the aloe vera leaf. Aloe

<!-- chunk -->

### is extremely soothing to irritated skin and mucous membranes, burns, and other

<!-- chunk -->

### damaged tissues.

<!-- chunk -->

### Whole leaf aloe vera juice builds the immune system to help fight arthritis,

<!-- chunk -->

### AIDS, cancer, and other degenerative diseases.

<!-- chunk -->

### Aloe vera gel may be applied topically for burns and skin irritations. Apply

<!-- chunk -->

### liberally and keep the skin moist for best results. Aloe vera works best when

<!-- chunk -->

### fresh. Aloe plants are easy to grow and keep in the home for treating burns.

<!-- chunk -->

### The outer leaf contains anthraquinone glycosides and is a strong purgative and

<!-- chunk -->

### stimulant laxative. This is filtered out when extracting the juice and gel.


<!-- chunk -->

### Some herbalists suggest that children, the elderly, and pregnant

<!-- chunk -->

### women should not drink aloe vera juice. However, this may apply only to the

<!-- chunk -->

### green outer leaf portion (which is strongly cathartic) or to aloe vera concentrates.

<!-- chunk -->

### The diluted pulp juice is a mild, harmless remedy.


<!-- chunk -->

### Anti-inflammatory, antiseptic, demulcent (mucilant), emollient,

<!-- chunk -->

### stimulant laxative, purgative (cathartic), soothing, and vulnerary


<!-- chunk -->

### Hot and dry conditions, sunburns, inflammatory bowel

<!-- chunk -->

### disease, gastroparesis


# FRESH:

<!-- chunk -->

### Cut fresh leaf to expose the gel. Apply gel topically.

# CAPSULE (LEAF):

<!-- chunk -->

### 250–450 mg of the leaf extract daily as a laxative. Not for long-

<!-- chunk -->

### term use.

# JUICE (PULP ONLY):

<!-- chunk -->

### 1–4 ounces of the juice daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Apply juice or gel topically as needed.

# ANDROGRAPHIS

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Andrographis paniculata

<!-- chunk -->

### Andrographis is a potent antiviral, antibacterial, and immune stimulator.

<!-- chunk -->

### Andrographis extracts have been shown to mildly inhibit Staphylococcus aureus,

<!-- chunk -->

### Pseudomonas aeruginosa, Proteus vulgaris, Shigella dysenteriae, and Escherichia

<!-- chunk -->

### coli. Extracts have also been shown to inhibit lipid peroxidation and

<!-- chunk -->

### inflammation. It is used in Ayurvedic medicine for diarrhea, dyspepsia, lack of

<!-- chunk -->

### bile flow, hepatitis, pneumonia, tonsillitis, colds, sinus infections, and flu; and is

<!-- chunk -->

### used by modern herbalists to treat intestinal parasites, colds, influenza, and

<!-- chunk -->

### hepatitis. In a clinical study, patients treated with andrographis for 3 months

<!-- chunk -->

### were two times less likely to catch colds than the placebo group.


<!-- chunk -->

### Not for use during pregnancy or lactation


<!-- chunk -->

### Anti-inflammatory, antibacterial, bitter, cholagogue, febrifuge, and

<!-- chunk -->

### immune stimulant


<!-- chunk -->

### ½ cup 3–4 times daily. Tastes too bad for most people to

<!-- chunk -->

### drink.


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried leaf (1:5, 50% alcohol); 1–4 ml (0.2–0.8 tsp.) 3–4 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried leaf (1:8); 5–10 ml (1–2 tsp.) 3–4 times daily


# ANGELICA

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Angelica archangelica

<!-- chunk -->

### Angelica is a warming aromatic tonic useful for many ailments. Angelica helps

<!-- chunk -->

### to warm a cold, stiff, weakened body and is especially warming to the stomach,

<!-- chunk -->

### spleen, and intestines. This makes it helpful for poor digestion, colic, and

<!-- chunk -->

### intestinal cramps. It promotes perspiration, making it useful for reducing fever. It

<!-- chunk -->

### also helps recovery from colds, flu, and congestion in the lungs. Angelica is

<!-- chunk -->

### related to dong quai and has similar actions; it is a valuable remedy for women

<!-- chunk -->

### that helps to regulate menses and balance hormones. It is an uplifting remedy

<!-- chunk -->

### and can be helpful for stagnant depression. It can also be applied externally for

<!-- chunk -->

### bruises, sprains, and muscle and joint pain.


<!-- chunk -->

### Not for use during pregnancy or while nursing. Also contraindicated

<!-- chunk -->

### in heavy menstrual bleeding.


<!-- chunk -->

### Aromatic, decongestant, and digestive tonic


<!-- chunk -->

### King’s American Dispensatory: Flatulent colic and

<!-- chunk -->

### heartburn, and nervous headache.


<!-- chunk -->

### Fresh root (1:2, 95% alcohol); dried root (1:5, 65% alcohol); 1–3 ml

<!-- chunk -->

### (0.2–0.6 tsp.) 3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:5); 2–5 ml (0.4–1 tsp.) 3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### 1 500 mg capsule 3 times daily (doesn’t work on digestion; only for

<!-- chunk -->

### pelvic circulation)

# ANISE

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Pimpinella anisum

<!-- chunk -->

### Anise is a soothing aromatic with properties similar to those of fennel. Tea,

<!-- chunk -->

### tincture, or oil can be used to settle the stomach and expel gas. It is useful for

<!-- chunk -->

### colic in infants and helps promote lactation for the breastfeeding mother. It is a

<!-- chunk -->

### mucolytic agent, helping to thin mucus and expel it from the lungs. It is a

<!-- chunk -->

### common ingredient in formulas for indigestion, but is not a key herb in these

<!-- chunk -->

### formulas.


<!-- chunk -->

### Anise is a traditional abortifacient. There are no reports of it being

<!-- chunk -->

### harmful when used in normal food doses, but avoid medicinal doses when

<!-- chunk -->

### pregnant except under the supervision of a well-trained herbalist.


<!-- chunk -->

### Aromatic, carminative, and galactagogue


<!-- chunk -->

### King’s American Dispensatory: Flatulency, flatulent colic

<!-- chunk -->

### of infants, and to remove nausea.


<!-- chunk -->

### Mountain Rose Herbs, San Francisco Herb Company, Starwest


<!-- chunk -->

### 2–8 ounces 2–3 times daily. For gastrointestinal complaints in

<!-- chunk -->

### children, give 1 ounce as needed, sweetened with maple syrup. For infants, add

<!-- chunk -->

### teaspoon to their bottle, or give breastfeeding mothers strong doses.


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried (1:5, 50% alcohol and 10% glycerin); 1–3 ml (0.2–0.6 tsp.)


<!-- chunk -->

### Sealed simmer dried (1:8); 2–5 ml (0.4–1 tsp.) 3 times daily

# ARNICA

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Arnica montana

<!-- chunk -->

### Arnica is used to reduce swelling, bruising, and pain from injury and trauma. It

<!-- chunk -->

### is most often used as a homeopathic preparation both internally and topically to

<!-- chunk -->

### treat swelling, bruises, and injuries. It is a good idea to keep homeopathic arnica

<!-- chunk -->

### (both tablets and topical cream) in your first aid kit.

<!-- chunk -->

### Taken internally, arnica tincture has an even stronger anti-inflammatory action

<!-- chunk -->

### than the homeopathic preparation. In higher doses it acts as a cardiac tonic and

<!-- chunk -->

### improves the supply of blood through the coronary vessels. Arnica tincture is

<!-- chunk -->

### toxic and should be taken only under professional supervision. It should be

<!-- chunk -->

### highly diluted when used internally—just a few drops in a cup of water.


<!-- chunk -->

### Gastric irritation may develop with internal use of the herb. High

<!-- chunk -->

### doses taken internally can cause intoxication, dizziness, tremors, tachycardia,

<!-- chunk -->

### arrhythmia, and collapse. Arnica tincture should not be used during pregnancy or

<!-- chunk -->

### nursing. Homeopathic preparations do not cause these problems, but neither the

<!-- chunk -->

### herb nor the homeopathic preparation should be applied to broken skin. Arnica

<!-- chunk -->

### contains sesquiterpene lactones that can produce contact dermatitis in sensitive

<!-- chunk -->

### persons.


<!-- chunk -->

### Analgesic (anodyne), anticoagulant (blood thinner), vasodilator,

<!-- chunk -->

### and vulnerary


<!-- chunk -->

### Rolla Thomas: Tensive pain in the back as if bruised or

<!-- chunk -->

### strained; muscular pain and soreness when the limbs are moved; feeble

<!-- chunk -->

### respiration.


<!-- chunk -->

### Fresh leaf or root (1:2, 70% alcohol); dried leaf (1:5, 50% alcohol); 1–

<!-- chunk -->

### 5 drops in 8 ounces of water, sipped slowly, up to 3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Apply tincture, ointment, or oil topically to unbroken skin as

<!-- chunk -->

### needed.

# ARTICHOKE

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Cynara scolymus

<!-- chunk -->

### This is the leaf of the globe artichoke that is eaten as a vegetable. It contains

<!-- chunk -->

### cynarin, which has proven liver protection capabilities. Artichoke leaf also

<!-- chunk -->

### contains silymarin, the active constituent of milk thistle. The leaves are used as a

<!-- chunk -->

### digestive bitter for a sluggish liver and poor digestion.


<!-- chunk -->

### People with an existing hypersensitivity to any member of the

<!-- chunk -->

### Asteraceae family should use caution.


<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### and digestive tonic

<!-- chunk -->

### Dried leaf (1:8); 1–5 ml (0.2–1 tsp.) 3 times daily

# ASHWAGANDHA

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Withania somnifera

<!-- chunk -->

### An important herb from Ayurvedic medicine, ashwagandha is a nervine and

<!-- chunk -->

### adrenal tonic that helps anxiety, depression, exhaustion, and poor muscle tone. It

<!-- chunk -->

### is adaptogenic and reduces the effects of stress while promoting energy and

<!-- chunk -->

### vitality. It is used as a supporting herb for recovery from debilitating diseases. It

<!-- chunk -->

### is effective for treating sexual dysfunction caused by stress. It is also an effective

<!-- chunk -->

### anti-inflammatory that can relieve symptoms associated with arthritis pain.

<!-- chunk -->

### Ashwagandha helps boost the conversion of T4 (the thyroid storage hormone) to

<!-- chunk -->

### T3 (the active thyroid hormone).


<!-- chunk -->

### Use cautiously during pregnancy. Contraindicated in those with

<!-- chunk -->

### sensitivity to the nightshade family.

### Slightly warming


<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### vanilla and honey

# BARBERRY

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Berberis vulgaris or B. aristata

<!-- chunk -->

### One of the best bitter liver tonics, barberry contains berberine, an antimicrobial

<!-- chunk -->

### and antifungal compound. Barberry has been shown to increase bile production

<!-- chunk -->

### and is one of the most useful cholagogues. Barberry also contains a compound

<!-- chunk -->

### called 5′-MHC, which helps keep bacteria from developing resistance to

<!-- chunk -->

### antibiotics, making it useful for many infections. Barberry is a common

<!-- chunk -->

### ingredient in blood purifying formulas.


<!-- chunk -->

### Not for use during pregnancy or when emaciated


<!-- chunk -->

### Alterative (blood purifier), antiseptic, aperient, bitter, and

<!-- chunk -->

### cholagogue


<!-- chunk -->

### Fyfe: Chronic blood dyscrasia (imbalance), with scaly

<!-- chunk -->

### skin eruptions and impaired nutrition and waste.


<!-- chunk -->

### 4 ounces 3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Fresh root (1:2, 95% alcohol); dried root (1:5, 50% alcohol); 1–4 ml

<!-- chunk -->

### (0.2–0.8 tsp.) 4 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:5); 1–5 ml (0.2–1 tsp.) 3–4 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### infections, apply a salve to the skin 3 times daily. Barberry will stain whatever it

<!-- chunk -->

### comes in contact with, including skin.

# BEE POLLEN

<!-- chunk -->

### Bee pollen contains every known nutrient in trace amounts. It is highly

<!-- chunk -->

### energizing and used to increase stamina and endurance. It supports the glands

<!-- chunk -->

### and aids the immune system. Bee pollen has been used to overcome allergies to

<!-- chunk -->

### pollen. It is best to get bee pollen from local beekeepers and start with a small

<!-- chunk -->

### amount (just a few grains). Gradually increase the dose over a period of several

<!-- chunk -->

### weeks to develop a tolerance to pollen and improve immune function.


<!-- chunk -->

### A few allergic reactions have been reported from the use of bee

<!-- chunk -->

### pollen. Symptoms of allergy include itching, dizziness, and difficulty

<!-- chunk -->

### swallowing. If you have allergies, be sure to start with a few grains.


<!-- chunk -->

### Neutral and nourishing


<!-- chunk -->

### Nutritive and metabolic stimulant


<!-- chunk -->

### Mountain Rose Herbs, San Francisco Herb Company, Starwest


<!-- chunk -->

### Bee pollen granules are gathered from the bees’ legs as they reenter the

<!-- chunk -->

### hive, and are sold as granules or are ground into powder. For general health

<!-- chunk -->

### purposes, take 1–2 heaping teaspoons of the raw granules daily. Mix them in

<!-- chunk -->

### juice, a smoothie, yogurt, applesauce, or cereal, or simply chew and swallow.


<!-- chunk -->

### 2–4 capsules (1,000–2,000 mg) up to 4 times daily.

# BILBERRY

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Vaccinium myrtillus

<!-- chunk -->

### Bilberries have been shown to improve night vision and help heal eye irritations.

<!-- chunk -->

### They contain anthocyanidins, which protect collagen structures in the eyes,

<!-- chunk -->

### thereby preventing and treating macular degeneration and retinopathy. Bilberries

<!-- chunk -->

### tone blood vessels and improve circulation. Studies suggest that the antioxidants

<!-- chunk -->

### in bilberries can protect against diseases of the circulatory system. Blueberry is a

<!-- chunk -->

### cousin of bilberry and can be used interchangeably. Blueberries and bilberries

<!-- chunk -->

### can improve atherosclerosis and varicose veins.


<!-- chunk -->

### None known for the fruit; long-term use of the leaves can potentially

<!-- chunk -->

### cause gastric irritation and kidney damage, but they have a history of safe use.


<!-- chunk -->

### Cooling, slightly drying, and nourishing


<!-- chunk -->

### Nutritive and vascular tonic


<!-- chunk -->

### The fresh berries can be eaten daily.


<!-- chunk -->

### 2–5 grams 3 times daily

# SOLID EXTRACT:

<!-- chunk -->

### Fresh berries can be cooked down and preserved with glycerin to

<!-- chunk -->

### make a solids extract. Take 1 teaspoon 2 times daily.


<!-- chunk -->

### Juice berries, warm, and mix with an equal part honey. Refrigerate or

<!-- chunk -->

### can.

# BITTER MELON

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Momordica charantia

<!-- chunk -->

### Bitter melon has long been used in Ayurvedic medicine to treat type 2 diabetes.

<!-- chunk -->

### It protects the pancreas, improves insulin resistance, and lowers blood lipids.

<!-- chunk -->

### Compounds in the plant inhibit Helicobacter pylori, which is useful in cases of

<!-- chunk -->

### gastric ulcers. Bitter melon may be helpful for parasites, intestinal worms, and

<!-- chunk -->

### stomach pain or colic accompanied by constipation.


<!-- chunk -->

### May cause diarrhea, stomachache, and bloating. Do not take with

<!-- chunk -->

### diabetes medications without professional supervision.


<!-- chunk -->

### Anthelminthic, antibacterial, anticancer, antidiabetic, antioxidant,

<!-- chunk -->

### antiviral, and bitter


# CULINARY:

<!-- chunk -->

### Eaten in traditional Asian cuisine. For most Americans this isn’t a

<!-- chunk -->

### pleasant-tasting food.


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried fruit (1:5, 50% alcohol); 2–4 ml (0.4–0.8 tsp.) up to 4 times


<!-- chunk -->

### 1–3 capsules (500–1,500 mg) up to 3 times daily

# JUICE EXTRACT:

<!-- chunk -->

### 2 ounces daily

# BLACK COHOSH

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Cimicifuga racemosa; Actaea racemosa

<!-- chunk -->

### Black cohosh is typically used for its estrogenic effects, but its role as a source

<!-- chunk -->

### of natural estrogens is questionable. It does seem to help with menopausal

<!-- chunk -->

### symptoms. Black cohosh is antispasmodic and mildly analgesic. It is a good

<!-- chunk -->

### remedy for venomous bites and stings. Black cohosh can help lower blood

<!-- chunk -->

### pressure, reduce joint inflammation, and enhance circulation. It helps improve

<!-- chunk -->

### dark, gloomy depression, and relieves dark, twisted emotional congestion.


<!-- chunk -->

### Black cohosh stimulates uterine contractions. It is contraindicated in

<!-- chunk -->

### early pregnancy but can be used (especially as part of a formula) during the last

<!-- chunk -->

### weeks of pregnancy or during labor.

<!-- chunk -->

### In large doses, black cohosh can cause headaches, dizziness, irritation of the

<!-- chunk -->

### central nervous system, nausea, and vomiting. If headache or dizziness occurs,

<!-- chunk -->

### reduce dose or discontinue use. When black cohosh is used in a formula, it is

<!-- chunk -->

### unlikely to cause any of these effects, because the dose is too low. Black cohosh

<!-- chunk -->

### headaches can often be remedied with a strong cup of green tea.


<!-- chunk -->

### Analgesic (anodyne), anti-arrhythmic, antidepressant,

<!-- chunk -->

### antirheumatic, antispasmodic, antivenomous, emmenagogue, and hypotensive


<!-- chunk -->

### Rolla Thomas: Muscular pains; uterine pain with

<!-- chunk -->

### tenderness; false pains; irregular pains; rheumatism of the uterus; dysmenorrhea.

<!-- chunk -->

### An antirheumatic when the pulse is open, the pain paroxysmal, the skin not dry

<!-- chunk -->

### and constricted.


<!-- chunk -->

### 2–4 ounces up to 3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Fresh root (1:2, 80% alcohol); dried root (1:5, 80% alcohol); 3–30

<!-- chunk -->

### drops (0.1–1 ml) 3 times daily; fresh root tincture is vastly superior to dried root.


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:5); 6 drops to 1 ml (0.2 tsp.) 3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### ½–1 capsule (250–500 mg) 2–3 times daily. Difficult to effectively

<!-- chunk -->

### regulate dosage with capsules.

# BLACK HAW

## Latin name: Viburnum prunifolium

### Black haw is an antispasmodic used to relieve painful menstruation and low

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

# BLACK PEPPER

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Piper nigrum

<!-- chunk -->

### Pepper is the world’s most traded spice and has been used since ancient times for

<!-- chunk -->

### culinary and medicinal purposes. It stimulates digestion and intestinal mobility

<!-- chunk -->

### to ease gas and bloating. It increases the activity of transport proteins at the tight

<!-- chunk -->

### gap junctions in the gut, which helps larger compounds like curcumin and

<!-- chunk -->

### berberine absorb better.


<!-- chunk -->

### Large doses can cause gastrointestinal irritation in some people.


<!-- chunk -->

### Warming and slightly drying


<!-- chunk -->

### Antiseptic, carminative, and circulatory stimulant


<!-- chunk -->

### Bulk Herb Store, San Francisco Herb Company, Stony Mountain

# BLACK WALNUT

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Juglans nigra

<!-- chunk -->

### Black walnut hulls are a locally acting antifungal and antimicrobial, excellent for

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### traditional remedy for hypothyroidism, probably acting on autoimmunity

<!-- chunk -->

### through gut bacteria regulation. Externally, it can be applied to athlete’s foot,

<!-- chunk -->

### ringworm, boils, and infected wounds. It builds tooth enamel when used as a

<!-- chunk -->

### tooth powder.

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### than the hulls.

<!-- chunk -->

# BLADDERWRACK

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Fucus vesiculosus

<!-- chunk -->

### Bladderwrack is a seaweed. It contains iodine, alginic acid, and fucoidan. Iodine

<!-- chunk -->

### is an essential mineral for the thyroid, uterus, breasts, and prostate. Alginic acid

<!-- chunk -->

### is a special type of fiber that can help acid reflux and acts as a mild appetite

<!-- chunk -->

### suppressant. Fucoidan is a compound shown to reduce inflammation and

<!-- chunk -->

### improve arthritis, diabetes, and other inflammatory conditions. Fucoidan is

<!-- chunk -->

### known to have a variety of antitumor and antiangiogenic properties.


<!-- chunk -->

### Not for use with hyperthyroidism or Graves’ disease. Use cautiously

<!-- chunk -->

### with Hashimoto’s thyroiditis and during pregnancy.


<!-- chunk -->

### Anti-inflammatory, antirheumatic, and nutritive


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried seaweed (1:3, 45% alcohol); 1–3 ml (0.2–0.6 tsp.) up to 4 times


<!-- chunk -->

### 1,000–2,000 mg, 2 times daily

# BLOODROOT

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Sanguinaria canadensis

<!-- chunk -->

### Bloodroot is an antimicrobial expectorant for chronic lung infections. It is a very

<!-- chunk -->

### powerful lymph-moving herb, normally used as part of a formula for chronically

<!-- chunk -->

### swollen lymph nodes. Externally it is used for fungal infections, eczema, skin

<!-- chunk -->

### disorders, skin cancers, ringworm, scabies, warts, and venereal sores.


<!-- chunk -->

### Used internally in very small doses. Large doses can cause nausea,

<!-- chunk -->

### vomiting, headaches, and respiratory failure. Do not use during pregnancy. For

<!-- chunk -->

### use under professional supervision only.


<!-- chunk -->

### Drying and cooling


<!-- chunk -->

### Antifungal, antiseptic, bitter, and lymphatic


<!-- chunk -->

### Fyfe: Burning, itching of throat; air passages hot, dry, and

<!-- chunk -->

### swollen. Sense of constriction in throat, difficult deglutition. Bronchial irritation

<!-- chunk -->

### with increased secretion. Uneasiness and burning in stomach.


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:10, 60% alcohol); 1–5 drops up to 3 times daily. Larger

<!-- chunk -->

### doses can be heating and irritating. Start small and don’t exceed 20 drops daily.

# BLUE COHOSH

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Caulophyllum thalictroides

<!-- chunk -->

### Herbalists use the herb in small doses over a period of time to induce delayed

<!-- chunk -->

### labor. This also works for inducing delayed menstruation. Taken during labor,

<!-- chunk -->

### blue cohosh strengthens contractions and eases the pain of childbirth. Its tonic

<!-- chunk -->

### action stimulates and relaxes the uterus at the same time, making it helpful for

<!-- chunk -->

### relieving painful menstrual symptoms such as cramps and breast pain. It can also

<!-- chunk -->

### be used to help ovarian pain.


<!-- chunk -->

### Because it stimulates uterine contractions, it should be avoided by

<!-- chunk -->

### pregnant women or women who are trying to become pregnant. It should also be

<!-- chunk -->

### avoided during heavy menstrual bleeding. It can be used by women after their

<!-- chunk -->

### due date to induce labor, but professional supervision is advised. Blue cohosh is

<!-- chunk -->

### mildly toxic in large doses.


<!-- chunk -->

### Cooling, drying, and relaxing


<!-- chunk -->

### Antispasmodic, emmenagogue, and oxytocic


<!-- chunk -->

### Felter: Uterine heaviness and sense of soreness in legs,

<!-- chunk -->

### with pelvic congestion. Sluggish labor pains.


<!-- chunk -->

### ½–1 cup 3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:5, 60% alcohol); 0.5–2 ml (0.1–0.4 tsp.) up to 4 times


<!-- chunk -->

### 500 mg, 2 times daily

# BLUE FLAG

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Iris versicolor

<!-- chunk -->

### This powerful liver cleansing herb is best used in small doses or as part of a

<!-- chunk -->

### combination. It is considered helpful for chronic skin diseases and gallbladder

<!-- chunk -->

### problems involving a lack of bile flow. It helps with hypoglycemia associated

<!-- chunk -->

### with migraines, sugar cravings, and red-colored skin.


<!-- chunk -->

### The fresh root is too strong for internal use and can be toxic. Only

<!-- chunk -->

### the dried herb should be used. Large doses of the dried herb can cause nausea,

<!-- chunk -->

### vomiting, intestinal pain, and diarrhea. Not for use during pregnancy or

<!-- chunk -->

### lactation.


<!-- chunk -->

### Bitter, cholagogue, emetic, and lymphatic


<!-- chunk -->

### Felter: Enlarged, soft, yielding lymphatic tissue.

<!-- chunk -->

### Gastrointestinal irritation, burning in the epigastrium, acid eructations.


<!-- chunk -->

### 1 ounce 2–3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:5, 50% alcohol); 1–10 drops 2 times daily

# BLUE VERVAIN

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Verbena hastata (blue vervain), V. officinalis (vervain)

<!-- chunk -->

### Blue vervain can be used internally to relax the nerves and combat anxiety. It is

<!-- chunk -->

### very helpful for nervous exhaustion from long-term stress or fanatical, hard-

<!-- chunk -->

### driving personalities and for people who suffer from neck and shoulder pain who

<!-- chunk -->

### feel like they’re tied up in knots. It’s helpful for women who get angry and tense

<!-- chunk -->

### just before their period, and for anger in general. It can alleviate some types of

<!-- chunk -->

### headaches, including migraines associated with PMS.

<!-- chunk -->

### Detail-oriented people who suffer from surface and peripheral nervous system

<!-- chunk -->

### problems and have neuralgias and skin problems may also benefit from blue

<!-- chunk -->

### vervain. It is helpful for many spasmodic nervous disorders, including tics,

<!-- chunk -->

### palsy, and Tourette’s syndrome. It can be helpful for mild pain and colds, flu,

<!-- chunk -->

### and respiratory congestion.


<!-- chunk -->

### Extremely large doses may cause nausea and vomiting. Large doses

<!-- chunk -->

### may stimulate a miscarriage in pregnant women, although in normal doses blue

<!-- chunk -->

### vervain was used traditionally to protect against miscarriage.


<!-- chunk -->

### Slightly cooling, drying, and relaxing


<!-- chunk -->

### Bitter, diaphoretic, diuretic, expectorant, hypotensive, nervine, and

<!-- chunk -->

### relaxant


<!-- chunk -->

### For nervine properties, 1 cup up to 3 times daily

# BONESET

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Eupatorium perfoliatum

<!-- chunk -->

### Boneset is an aromatic and bitter herb traditionally used for colds, fevers, and

<!-- chunk -->

### flu. Studies show that compounds in boneset stimulate white blood cell action. It

<!-- chunk -->

### is very helpful for flu accompanied by aches in the muscles. Taken as a warm

<!-- chunk -->

### tea, it helps to promote perspiration and acts as an emetic. Taken as a cold tea (a

<!-- chunk -->

### standard infusion that has been left to cool), it acts as a bitter tonic and mild

<!-- chunk -->

### laxative to strengthen and tone the bowels. It helps to relieve vomiting and

<!-- chunk -->

### bloating when combined with mint, and when combined with ginger and anise it

<!-- chunk -->

### aids coughs.


<!-- chunk -->

### Use cautiously during pregnancy. Long-term use is not

<!-- chunk -->

### recommended.


<!-- chunk -->

### Cooling, drying, and slightly relaxing


<!-- chunk -->

### Bitter, diaphoretic, and emetic


<!-- chunk -->

### Felter: Large, full pulse, current showing small waves,

<!-- chunk -->

### skin hot and full, with tendency to moisture. Deep-seated aching in bones with

<!-- chunk -->

### general body aches. Hoarseness, cough, soreness of chest. Urine turbid and high.


<!-- chunk -->

### 4–8 ounces, hot, 3–5 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

# BOSWELLIA

## Latin name: Boswellia serrata; also called frankincense

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

# BUTTERBUR ROOT

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Petasites hybridus

<!-- chunk -->

### This herb was tested on hay fever (allergic rhinitis) symptoms and found to be as

<!-- chunk -->

### effective as many OTC and prescription drugs. Butterbur has also been shown to

<!-- chunk -->

### reduce the frequency, intensity, and duration of migraines. It is a useful remedy

<!-- chunk -->

### for cramps and asthma.


<!-- chunk -->

### The plant contains pyrrolizidine alkaloids, which can be toxic to the

<!-- chunk -->

### liver. Some commercial extracts claim to remove the PAs, but the jury is still out.

<!-- chunk -->

### To be safe, limit use to 6 weeks a year.


<!-- chunk -->

### Analgesic (anodyne), anti-allergenic, antitussive, and expectorant


<!-- chunk -->

### There is no commercially available source of bulk butterbur that is PA-free.

<!-- chunk -->

### Until there is, we recommend you stick to the standardized PA-free products.


<!-- chunk -->

# BUTTERNUT BARK

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### buckthorn. As with cascara and buckthorn, the bark should be dried for a year

<!-- chunk -->

### before use. The laxative effects are dependent on gut bacteria and take effect 6–8

<!-- chunk -->

### hours after ingestion. A dose in the evening normally produces defecation upon

<!-- chunk -->

### arising in the morning. The unripe nut is used to kill intestinal worms.

<!-- chunk -->

### digestion. It may be thought of as a remedy in chronic eczema.

# CAPSICUM (CAYENNE)

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Capsicum frutescens or C. annuum

<!-- chunk -->

### Capsicum is a major stimulant for the circulatory system. It increases circulation

<!-- chunk -->

### to every area of the body it comes in contact with, internally or externally.

<!-- chunk -->

### Capsicum also strengthens the heartbeat. Capsicum is useful for shock, heart

<!-- chunk -->

### attack, and trauma. Because adequate blood supply is necessary for all tissues to

<!-- chunk -->

### heal, capsicum has earned a reputation in the West as a kind of cure-all. It is

<!-- chunk -->

### analgesic: the capsaicin in capsicum depletes substance P and thereby partially

<!-- chunk -->

### blocks pain receptors. A small part of capsicum is commonly added to formulas

<!-- chunk -->

### made in the Thomsonian and Physiomedicalism systems as an accelerant.


<!-- chunk -->

### Due to its irritating nature, some people have a hard time taking

<!-- chunk -->

### capsicum. Large doses can be irritating to the stomach and cause painful bowel

<!-- chunk -->

### eliminations. Although capsicum stops bleeding and has been used to heal

<!-- chunk -->

### ulcers, this herb can cause pain when used for these purposes; hence, it should be

<!-- chunk -->

### used with caution. It is best to start with extremely small doses to build up

<!-- chunk -->

### tolerance. When applied locally, capsicum causes burning sensations in sensitive

<!-- chunk -->

### areas such as genitals, sinuses, and eyes. It is not recommended for people with

<!-- chunk -->

### hemorrhoids or anal fissures. Topical use may exacerbate coughs caused by ACE

<!-- chunk -->

### inhibitors.


<!-- chunk -->

### Analgesic (anodyne), carminative, counterirritant, diaphoretic,

<!-- chunk -->

### hemostatic, circulatory stimulant, and styptic


<!-- chunk -->

### Felter: Marked depression with feeble pulse and scanty

<!-- chunk -->

### secretions. Tongue dry and harsh, salivary secretions suppressed.


<!-- chunk -->

### Fresh fruit (1:2, 95% alcohol); dried fruit (1:5, 60% alcohol); 5 drops

<!-- chunk -->

### to 1 ml (0.2 tsp.) in water, or, as a less irritating alternative, milk or coconut milk


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried fruit (1:5); 1–5 drops diluted in water or alternative

# CASCARA SAGRADA

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Rhamnus purshiana

<!-- chunk -->

### A bitter purgative, cascara sagrada increases bile flow and stimulates peristalsis

<!-- chunk -->

### of the colon. The name cascara sagrada means holy or sacred bark. It is known

<!-- chunk -->

### for its effectiveness in relieving constipation and for colon cleansing. The bark

<!-- chunk -->

### should be dried for 1 year before use. The correct dose is the smallest dose

<!-- chunk -->

### necessary to create soft stool.


<!-- chunk -->

### Not recommended for use during pregnancy or in those with

<!-- chunk -->

### inflammatory bowel disorders, abdominal pain, or obstruction. Avoid prolonged

<!-- chunk -->

### use. If a person appears dependent on this or other stimulant laxatives or if

<!-- chunk -->

### cramps or griping become a problem, use nervines for the dependency and

<!-- chunk -->

### bowel spasms, and use magnesium to counteract spasms. In case of diarrhea

<!-- chunk -->

### caused by excessive use, use charcoal or mucilaginous herbs. Long-term use will

<!-- chunk -->

### darken the tissue color of the bowel and create laxative dependency. Triphala is

<!-- chunk -->

### helpful for people who have become dependent on laxatives.


<!-- chunk -->

### Bitter, cholagogue, stimulant laxative, and purgative (cathartic)


<!-- chunk -->

### Felter: Constipation due to neglect, or to nervous or

<!-- chunk -->

### muscular atony of the bowels.


<!-- chunk -->

### 2–4 ounces at bedtime, but the taste is very unpleasant.


<!-- chunk -->

### Aged dried bark (1:5, 40% alcohol); 1–2 ml (0.2–0.4 tsp.) in a little

<!-- chunk -->

### water just before bedtime


<!-- chunk -->

### 500–1,000 mg, morning and/or evening

# CINNAMON

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Cinnamomum verum, syn. C. zeylanicum

<!-- chunk -->

### Cinnamon is a spicy aromatic herb used in traditional Chinese medicine as a

<!-- chunk -->

### warming stimulant. It is useful as a digestive and circulatory stimulant. Modern

<!-- chunk -->

### research has shown that cinnamon increases the capability of beta cells in the

<!-- chunk -->

### pancreas to produce insulin, reducing blood glucose levels in diabetics.

<!-- chunk -->

### Cinnamon also has astringent properties and can help control heavy menstrual

<!-- chunk -->

### flows and postpartum bleeding. Cinnamon is a strong antimicrobial and is

<!-- chunk -->

### helpful for certain types of dysbiosis. Cinnamon essential oil (Cassia variety) has

<!-- chunk -->

### powerful antibacterial and antifungal properties.


<!-- chunk -->

### Large amounts of cinnamon oil ingested internally can cause kidney

<!-- chunk -->

### damage or coma. Cinnamon oil and bark are not recommended during pregnancy

<!-- chunk -->

### except as a seasoning in food. It is a good idea to avoid cinnamon while

<!-- chunk -->

### breastfeeding. Taking more than 2 grams of cinnamon bark daily can cause

<!-- chunk -->

### gastrointestinal irritation.


<!-- chunk -->

### Warming, drying, and constricting


<!-- chunk -->

### Antidiabetic, antiseptic, aromatic, astringent, and carminative


<!-- chunk -->

### Felter: Passive hemorrhage. Gastric irritation with

<!-- chunk -->

### flatulence.


<!-- chunk -->

### Company

### Comfrey is a mucilaginous herb with a slight astringent quality. It has been used

<!-- chunk -->

### for generations to aid in the healing of injuries. Not only does it contain

<!-- chunk -->

### important minerals needed in the healing process, but it also contains allantoin, a

<!-- chunk -->

### substance that stimulates cell growth. Comfrey is primarily used externally in

<!-- chunk -->

### compresses, poultices, and salves. It has been used internally, but most herbalists

<!-- chunk -->

### no longer use it this way because of concerns about hepatic toxicity.


<!-- chunk -->

### Completely safe for topical use. It contains pyrrolizidine alkaloids,

<!-- chunk -->

### which are believed to cause liver problems when taken internally. Many people

<!-- chunk -->

### have used comfrey internally with no reported ill effects, and it is probably safe

<!-- chunk -->

### to use internally for short periods. It should be avoided during pregnancy,

<!-- chunk -->

### lactation, when cancer or tumors are present, or when there is a history of liver

<!-- chunk -->

### problems.


<!-- chunk -->

### Cooling, moistening, and slightly constricting


<!-- chunk -->

### Emollient and vulnerary


<!-- chunk -->

### Francisco Herb Company, Starwest Botanicals


<!-- chunk -->

### 4–8 ounces up to 3 times daily for no more than 6 weeks a

<!-- chunk -->

### year. We recommend the internal use of comfrey only for broken bones that

<!-- chunk -->

### don’t seem to be healing together naturally or with the assistance of safer herbs.


<!-- chunk -->

### Apply fresh or dried leaf as a poultice; a standard infusion as a

<!-- chunk -->

### compress or soak; or the oil or salve as needed

# CORDYCEPS

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Cordyceps sinensis, C. militaris

<!-- chunk -->

### Cordyceps entered Western medicine after the Chinese government

<!-- chunk -->

### demonstrated its efficacy at the 2008 Olympic games in Beijing, where the

<!-- chunk -->

### Chinese athletes set new world records in nearly every competition they entered.

<!-- chunk -->

### The spectacular performance of the athletes stimulated a burst of

<!-- chunk -->

### pharmacological and clinical research into its health benefits. Cordyceps is an

<!-- chunk -->

### adaptogen and general health tonic. It benefits the lungs, kidneys, adrenal

<!-- chunk -->

### glands, and cardiovascular system. Wildcrafted cordyceps is very difficult to

<!-- chunk -->

### find; when available, be sure it has been tested for heavy metals. Cultured Cs-4

<!-- chunk -->

### strain powder works well and is easier to find.


<!-- chunk -->

### Balancing and slightly warming


<!-- chunk -->

### Adaptogen, anti-inflammatory, anticancer, anticholesteremic,

<!-- chunk -->

### antioxidant, immune amphoteric, and tonic


<!-- chunk -->

### 5–10 grams daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried mushrooms (1:4, 25% alcohol); 2–4 ml (0.4–0.8 tsp.) 3 times


<!-- chunk -->

### 1,000–2,000 mg, 2–3 times daily

# CORYDALIS

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Corydalis yanhusuo

<!-- chunk -->

### Corydalis is a natural pain reliever. It contains an alkaloid called THP that acts

<!-- chunk -->

### similarly to opium poppy but is much milder. It is a central nervous system

<!-- chunk -->

### depressant and appropriate for pain from any cause. It has traditionally been

<!-- chunk -->

### used for pain associated with rheumatism, arthritis, or menstruation. It can also

<!-- chunk -->

### be used as an aid for sleep and anxiety.


<!-- chunk -->

### Warming and relaxing


<!-- chunk -->

### Analgesic (anodyne), sedative, and soporific (hypnotic)


<!-- chunk -->

### Tastes vile, but is effective. 3–8 ounces as needed


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried rhizome (1:3, 50% alcohol); 1–5 ml (0.2–1 tsp.) as needed


<!-- chunk -->

### THP 100–200 mg daily


<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### 3 times daily

# COTTON ROOT

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Gossypium herbaceum

<!-- chunk -->

### Cotton root is used for menstrual cramping with scanty bleeding. It can also be

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### lassitude with anemia; hysteria, with pelvic atony and anemia.

<!-- chunk -->

# CRANBERRY

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Vaccinium macrocarpon

<!-- chunk -->

### Cranberries contain antioxidants that mitigate the damaging effects of free

<!-- chunk -->

### radicals in the body. They also contain two compounds that prevent the

<!-- chunk -->

### adherence of E. coli to the bladder: mannose and proanthocyanidins. Cranberries

<!-- chunk -->

### are an effective preventative for urinary tract infections, and they also help treat

<!-- chunk -->

### H. pylori and gastric E. coli infections. They are high in vitamin C and have

<!-- chunk -->

### been used to prevent scurvy in sailors. Commercially prepared cranberry juice

<!-- chunk -->

### can be used; it works better if it has no added sugar.


<!-- chunk -->

### Antibacterial, antioxidant, and nutritive


# FRESH:

<!-- chunk -->

### Whole cranberries. Eat 1.5 ounces daily.

# JUICE:

<!-- chunk -->

### 3–8 ounces daily of unsweetened juice


<!-- chunk -->

### 1,000–3,000 mg, 2–3 times daily

# DANDELION

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Taraxacum officinale

<!-- chunk -->

### This common lawn and garden weed has a beneficial effect on the digestive

<!-- chunk -->

### system, the urinary system, and the pancreas. The root is primarily used to

<!-- chunk -->

### stimulate bile flow and aid the liver, whereas the leaf is more often employed as

<!-- chunk -->

### a diuretic to aid kidney function. It acts on the microflora of the gut and helps

<!-- chunk -->

### stimulate digestive secretions. Dandelion leaf is often combined in equal parts

<!-- chunk -->

### with nettle leaf as a potassium-sparing diuretic. Dandelion flower wine makes a

<!-- chunk -->

### nice digestive tonic.


<!-- chunk -->

### Alterative (blood purifier), bitter, cholagogue, digestive tonic,

<!-- chunk -->

### diuretic, hepatoprotective


# FRESH:

<!-- chunk -->

### Eat young spring leaves raw.


<!-- chunk -->

### Leaf: 4–8 ounces 3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

# ECHINACEA

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Echinacea angustifolia

<!-- chunk -->

### There are several species of echinacea used. We prefer Echinacea angustifolia, or

<!-- chunk -->

### a combination of E. angustifolia and E. purpurea. E. pallida lacks the alkamides

<!-- chunk -->

### that contribute to E. angustifolia’s and E. purpurea’s action. E. angustifolia is

<!-- chunk -->

### superior to E. purpurea for topical application to wounds, bites, and stings.

<!-- chunk -->

### Echinacea aids the process of antibody formation and stimulates the production

<!-- chunk -->

### of white blood cells. It helps to strengthen and clear lymph nodes. It inhibits

<!-- chunk -->

### hyaluronidase (an enzyme produced by bacteria that breaks down compounds

<!-- chunk -->

### that bind cells together), thus inhibiting the spread of infection. Echinacea also

<!-- chunk -->

### helps the body fight viral infections. Echinacea is a wonderful herb to use

<!-- chunk -->

### topically for infections. It is often used to treat colds and flu, but is actually not

<!-- chunk -->

### the best herb for this purpose. Due to its popularity, echinacea is probably

<!-- chunk -->

### overused for many applications when other herbs would be just as effective.


<!-- chunk -->

### Echinacea is nontoxic and mostly harmless. Use very cautiously if

<!-- chunk -->

### you have an autoimmune disorder. High-quality preparations of echinacea can

<!-- chunk -->

### cause excessive salivation and a scratchy, tingling sensation in the throat.


<!-- chunk -->

### Alterative (blood purifier), antiseptic, antivenomous, antiviral,

<!-- chunk -->

### immune stimulant, and lymphatic


<!-- chunk -->

### Felter: Systemic sepsis, tendency to boils and to formation

<!-- chunk -->

### of semiactive multiple cellular abscesses, with adynamia and asthenia. Foul

<!-- chunk -->

### discharges with emaciation. Dirty brownish or bluish tongue, with sordes. Skin

<!-- chunk -->

### and mucous membranes dull bluish or purplish in color.


<!-- chunk -->

### Fresh root for E. angustifolia, fresh herb for E. purpurea (1:2, 95%

<!-- chunk -->

### alcohol); dried root for E. angustifolia, dried herb for E. purpurea (1:5, 60%

<!-- chunk -->

### alcohol); 1–5 ml (0.2–1 tsp.) 3–6 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root or herb (1:5); 2–8 ml (0.4–1.6 tsp.)


<!-- chunk -->

### 400–1,200 mg, 3–4 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### A standard decoction or tincture can be used as a wash or

<!-- chunk -->

### compress.

# ELDER

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Sambucus canadensis, S. nigra

<!-- chunk -->

### Elder is a very versatile herb with many useful parts. Elder flowers are an

<!-- chunk -->

### excellent remedy for acute ailments. They help to promote perspiration and

<!-- chunk -->

### reduce inflammation. Research suggests they may have anti-inflammatory,

<!-- chunk -->

### antiviral, and anticancer properties, as well as the ability to shorten the duration

<!-- chunk -->

### and severity of flu symptoms. They work especially well in combination with

<!-- chunk -->

### yarrow and peppermint. They can also be used topically in skin lotions.

<!-- chunk -->

### The fruits (elder berries) have a mild laxative and decongestant action, and

<!-- chunk -->

### they inhibit the spread of many viral infections. The bark, although not

<!-- chunk -->

### commonly used now, was traditionally used as a laxative and to soothe mucous

<!-- chunk -->

### membranes.


<!-- chunk -->

### All parts of the fresh plant are mildly toxic and can cause nausea and

<!-- chunk -->

### diarrhea. Even dried, the stems, bark, and root contain enough residual

<!-- chunk -->

### compounds to induce nausea. The flowers should be dried before using. The

<!-- chunk -->

### berries should be used dried, or boil fresh berries for 3 minutes before

<!-- chunk -->

### preserving.


<!-- chunk -->

### Anti-inflammatory, antiviral, decongestant, diaphoretic, febrifuge,

<!-- chunk -->

### and nutritive


<!-- chunk -->

### Flowers: 4–8 ounces served hot as a diaphoretic up to


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried flowers (1:5, 60% alcohol); 1–3 ml (0.2–0.6 tsp.) 2–4 times


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried flowers (1:6, sealed simmer method); dried berries (1:5, sealed

<!-- chunk -->

### simmer method); 5–10 ml (1–2 tsp.) 4 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Cook fresh or dried berries with a little water until soft, then press

<!-- chunk -->

### through a jelly bag. Measure juice, add an equal amount of honey, bring to a

<!-- chunk -->

### boil, remove from heat, and refrigerate or can; 1–2 teaspoons 4 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Use salve made from flowers as needed.

# ELEUTHERO

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Eleutherococcus senticosus

<!-- chunk -->

### Eleuthero has had more than three thousand studies performed on it, more than

<!-- chunk -->

### any other herb in the world. It was the first plant identified as an adaptogen by

<!-- chunk -->

### Russian scientists. Not only does it help the body cope better with stress, but it

<!-- chunk -->

### also increases endurance and stimulates the brain to improve concentration.

<!-- chunk -->

### Soviet researchers found that eleuthero improved athletic performance, aided

<!-- chunk -->

### cosmonauts in preventing space sickness, caused secretaries to make fewer

<!-- chunk -->

### mistakes, and helped workers have fewer sick days. In other words, eleuthero

<!-- chunk -->

### enhances endurance, immunity, brain function, and general good health.

<!-- chunk -->

### Eleuthero is one of the more stimulating adaptogens and should be used short

<!-- chunk -->

### term, or in lower doses, to prevent overstimulation and insomnia.


<!-- chunk -->

### Insomnia and agitation can occur at higher doses or in sensitive

<!-- chunk -->

### people.


<!-- chunk -->

### Balancing and slightly warming


<!-- chunk -->

### Adaptogen, antirheumatic, hypotensive, and immune amphoteric


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root concentrate (2:1, 30% alcohol), 10 drops to 5 ml (1 tsp.) up

<!-- chunk -->

### to 3 times daily for short term; dried root (1:4, 30% alcohol), 1–3 ml (0.2–0.6

<!-- chunk -->

### tsp.) daily, normally as part of a formula


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:5); 5–10 ml (1–2 tsp.) 2–3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### 500–1,000 mg, 2–3 times daily

# EYEBRIGHT

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Euphrasia officinalis

<!-- chunk -->

### Eyebright is commonly used to treat eye infections and strengthen the eyes.

<!-- chunk -->

### Although it is commonly taken internally for these conditions, it works best

<!-- chunk -->

### when used as an eyewash. The best use of eyebright is as an internal remedy for

<!-- chunk -->

### upper respiratory congestion with acute irritation of the sinuses and eyes with

<!-- chunk -->

### thin, watery mucus and itching eyes and ears, such as rhinitis or the early stages

<!-- chunk -->

### of a cold. A tincture made from the fresh plant will open the Eustachian tubes in

<!-- chunk -->

### children, allowing the inner ear to drain and thus preventing earaches. The dried

<!-- chunk -->

### leaf is almost entirely ineffective for allergies and Eustachian tube issues.


<!-- chunk -->

### Eyebright tinctures used as eye drops can cause increased eye

<!-- chunk -->

### pressure, redness, watering, and swelling; when using eyebright topically, use

<!-- chunk -->

### the tea.


<!-- chunk -->

### Anti-allergenic, anti-inflammatory, astringent, and ophthalmicum


<!-- chunk -->

### Ellingwood: Acute irritating inflammation of mucous

<!-- chunk -->

### membranes of eyes and upper respiratory passages, with acrid, watery

<!-- chunk -->

### discharges.

### Frontier Herbs, Starwest Botanicals


<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### dried leaf. Apply as needed.

# FEVERFEW

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Tanacetum parthenium

<!-- chunk -->

### Feverfew is a popular natural remedy for migraine headaches. It does not work

<!-- chunk -->

### very well once the migraine has started, but when taken regularly it helps to

<!-- chunk -->

### prevent migraines and lessen their severity. Its name comes from its traditional

<!-- chunk -->

### use as a remedy for fevers. It is an effective small intestinal anti-inflammatory

<!-- chunk -->

### that combines well with chamomile and calendula for gastritis and leaky gut.


<!-- chunk -->

### Not for use during pregnancy. If mouth soreness or ulcerations

<!-- chunk -->

### develop, reduce dosage or discontinue use. It does not work on migraine

<!-- chunk -->

### headaches caused by weakness or deficiency (for example, anemia).


<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### nervine

### softener and bulk laxative for chronic constipation. Flax lignans are

<!-- chunk -->

### phytoestrogens and may be helpful in preventing estrogen-dependent cancers.


<!-- chunk -->

### Flaxseeds oxidize very rapidly after being ground. Grinding your

<!-- chunk -->

### own fresh flaxseeds as needed is best.


<!-- chunk -->

### Bulk laxative and phytoestrogen


<!-- chunk -->

### Grind whole flaxseeds in a coffee grinder and use fresh (flaxseed

<!-- chunk -->

### begins to oxidize within 20 minutes of grinding). Sprinkle on food or mix in

<!-- chunk -->

### liquid. Start with 1 teaspoon, and gradually work your way up to a dose of 2–3

<!-- chunk -->

### tablespoons 2 times daily.

# FRINGE TREE

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Chionanthus virginicus

<!-- chunk -->

### A bitter tonic with blood purifying, laxative, and mild diuretic actions, fringe

<!-- chunk -->

### tree is a very effective gallbladder remedy. It stimulates bile flow and helps

<!-- chunk -->

### relieve intestinal gas, bloating, and a stuffy feeling under the right rib cage. It is

<!-- chunk -->

### one of the best herbs for gallstones, especially when combined with other

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### Felter: Jaundice of skin and conjunctiva. Hepatic

<!-- chunk -->

# GARLIC

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Allium sativum

<!-- chunk -->

### Garlic is a strong aromatic herb that acts as an expectorant to expel phlegm from

<!-- chunk -->

### the lungs, and as a circulatory tonic to lower high blood pressure. It combines

<!-- chunk -->

### well with other herbs for treating certain bacterial and fungal infections. For

<!-- chunk -->

### hypertension, it must be taken daily for at least 3–6 months to see full results.

<!-- chunk -->

### The fresh bulb has the best anti-hypertensive and antimicrobial properties.


<!-- chunk -->

### Not for feeble, emaciated, or wasting conditions. Gastric irritation is

<!-- chunk -->

### possible; take with or after meals to lessen this effect.


<!-- chunk -->

### Anthelminthic, antibacterial, anticoagulant (blood thinner),

<!-- chunk -->

### antifungal, antiseptic, aromatic, decongestant, expectorant, and circulatory

<!-- chunk -->

### stimulant


<!-- chunk -->

### Finely mince 1 clove and take 3 times daily. If the taste is

<!-- chunk -->

### objectionable, add an equal amount of honey.


<!-- chunk -->

### Aged garlic capsules can slightly lower blood pressure, but are totally

<!-- chunk -->

### ineffective as an expectorant or antimicrobial.

# GHOST PIPE (INDIAN PIPE)

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Monotropa uniflora

<!-- chunk -->

### Ghost pipe is used primarily to help ease pain. It does not numb pain, but rather

<!-- chunk -->

### takes the pain, whether physical or emotional, outside of the mind so that you

<!-- chunk -->

### remain aware of the pain but no longer feel it. It can be helpful for panic attacks

<!-- chunk -->

### from emotional pain and bad trips from LSD. Ghost pipe is difficult to find and

<!-- chunk -->

### is impossible to grow because it parasitizes fungal mycorrhiza and has never

<!-- chunk -->

### been cultivated. Reserve its use for pain that doesn’t respond to anything else.


<!-- chunk -->

### Consumption of large doses can bring deep sleep and ultra-vivid

<!-- chunk -->

### dreams.


<!-- chunk -->

### Relaxing and cooling


<!-- chunk -->

### Antispasmodic, nervine, and sedative


<!-- chunk -->

### Fresh aboveground parts (1:2, 95% alcohol); 3 drops. If nothing

<!-- chunk -->

### happens after 10 minutes, gradually increase dose to 30 drops. Repeat effective

<!-- chunk -->

### dose every 2–4 hours as needed.

# GINGER

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Zingiber officinale

<!-- chunk -->

### A pungent aromatic, ginger is used to relieve nausea, vomiting, and motion

<!-- chunk -->

### sickness. Take capsules or the extract before traveling, to prevent motion

<!-- chunk -->

### sickness. It stimulates digestive secretions when taken with or after meals.

<!-- chunk -->

### Research indicates that ginger root enhances immune function, promotes the

<!-- chunk -->

### secretion of bile and gastric fluids, and increases blood circulation by inhibiting

<!-- chunk -->

### platelet aggregation. It is a potent anti-inflammatory, and studies show it is as

<!-- chunk -->

### effective as ibuprofen for reducing the pain and inflammation associated with

<!-- chunk -->

### arthritis. Fresh ginger is also a potent antiviral and antibacterial, helpful for

<!-- chunk -->

### treating influenza, the common cold, and both bacterial and viral gastroenteritis.


<!-- chunk -->

### Some authors caution against use during pregnancy, but no adverse

<!-- chunk -->

### effects have been reported by women using ginger for morning sickness.


<!-- chunk -->

### Analgesic (anodyne), anti-emetic (antinauseous), aromatic,

<!-- chunk -->

### carminative, counterirritant, diaphoretic, digestive tonic, and circulatory

<!-- chunk -->

### stimulant


# FRESH JUICE:

<!-- chunk -->

### Juice fresh and use 4 ounces, mixed with equal parts hot water,

<!-- chunk -->

### times daily. Add honey and lemon or lime to taste. You can freeze the fresh juice

<!-- chunk -->

### in ice cube trays for later use, or preserve by adding enough alcohol to bring the

<!-- chunk -->

### total alcohol content above 20% (25 ml of 95% alcohol and 75 ml fresh ginger

<!-- chunk -->

### juice).


<!-- chunk -->

### Preserve the fresh juice with 25% alcohol, 1–5 ml (0.2–1 tsp.) up to

<!-- chunk -->

### times daily; dried root (1:5, 60% alcohol), 0.8–1.5 ml (0.1–0.3 tsp.) in water


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:5, sealed simmer method), 1–3 ml (0.2–0.6 tsp.) in

<!-- chunk -->

### water as needed; preserve fresh juice with 50% glycerin, measure the total

<!-- chunk -->

### amount of liquid, and add 20% brandy or rum, ½–1 tsp. with water as needed


<!-- chunk -->

### 500–1,000 mg, as needed, up to 8 daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Taken as a food, ginger promotes digestive and general health.

# GINKGO

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Ginkgo biloba

<!-- chunk -->

### Extensive research has been conducted in Europe using concentrated extracts of

<!-- chunk -->

### the flavonoids in this herb. Ginkgo is best used as a standardized extract. It is

<!-- chunk -->

### commonly used to enhance memory and brain function. It improves blood flow

<!-- chunk -->

### to the brain and acts as an antioxidant to protect brain cells from damage. It also

<!-- chunk -->

### improves peripheral circulation and may be beneficial in diabetic retinopathy,

<!-- chunk -->

### tinnitus, vertigo, and dizziness. Best results are obtained when the herb is used

<!-- chunk -->

### consistently for 2–3 months. Ginkgo is an excellent remedy to take to slow the

<!-- chunk -->

### aging process and protect the nervous and cardiovascular systems.


<!-- chunk -->

### Use with caution when taking blood thinners. Safety during

<!-- chunk -->

### pregnancy hasn’t been established.


<!-- chunk -->

### Slightly cooling


<!-- chunk -->

### Anticoagulant (blood thinner), antioxidant, cerebral tonic,

<!-- chunk -->

### hypotensive, and vasodilator


<!-- chunk -->

### Concentration and standardization are required for

<!-- chunk -->

### therapeutic activity. There is no demonstrated therapeutic activity to the crude,

<!-- chunk -->

### powdered, tinctured, infused, or decocted leaf—only adverse allergic reactions

<!-- chunk -->

### to ginkgolic acid. The usual daily dose is 120 mg of a 50:1 ginkgo standardized

<!-- chunk -->

### extract, equivalent to 27–30 mg ginkgo flavone glycosides and about 10 mg

<!-- chunk -->

### terpenoids.

# GINSENG (AMERICAN)

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Panax quinquefolius

<!-- chunk -->

### American ginseng is used as a tonic for strengthening the overall system,

<!-- chunk -->

### improving stamina and resistance to disease. It helps counteract the effects of

<!-- chunk -->

### aging and improves overall health when taken in very small doses. American

<!-- chunk -->

### ginseng is less stimulating than Asian (Korean) ginseng. It helps regulate blood

<!-- chunk -->

### sugar, improves digestion, helps the body cope better with stress, and strengthens

<!-- chunk -->

### adrenal and general glandular function. Ginseng works best in small doses.


<!-- chunk -->

### Not toxic, but should not be taken by persons with high blood

<!-- chunk -->

### pressure, fevers, acute inflammation, or acute diseases like colds and flu.

<!-- chunk -->

### Regular large doses can cause insomnia and nervous overstimulation.


<!-- chunk -->

### Adaptogen, adrenal tonic, antidiabetic, hypertensive, and tonic


<!-- chunk -->

### Rolla Thomas: Nervous dyspepsia; sensation of dullness

<!-- chunk -->

### in head, with inability to control the voluntary muscles.


<!-- chunk -->

### Mountain Rose Herbs, Stony Mountain Botanicals


<!-- chunk -->

### For weakened people, 2–10 grams daily as a decoction

<!-- chunk -->

### can be used for 2–3 days to speed up recovery from acute illness. Don’t give this

<!-- chunk -->

### dose if there are any heat signs.


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:4, 30% alcohol); 2–5 drops 1–3 times daily for long-

<!-- chunk -->

### term use


<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### normally all that is needed as a long-term tonic.

# GINSENG (ASIAN, KOREAN)

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Panax ginseng

<!-- chunk -->

### Ginseng is one of the most highly prized herbs in the world. Asian or Korean

<!-- chunk -->

### ginseng has been shown to increase energy, help fight fatigue, and increase

<!-- chunk -->

### physical stamina and agility. It may even enhance the body’s ability to recover

<!-- chunk -->

### from physical injuries. Small doses of ginseng are used to slow aging, reduce

<!-- chunk -->

### stress, balance mood, and enhance a person’s general health. Ginseng may lower

<!-- chunk -->

### the risk of cancer and build up a weakened immune system. Asian ginseng is

<!-- chunk -->

### more warming than American ginseng and is well suited to older men and

<!-- chunk -->

### women who tend to be cold, pale, and easily fatigued. Red ginseng, which is

<!-- chunk -->

### steamed before drying, is more warming in energy, whereas white ginseng,

<!-- chunk -->

### which is just peeled and dried, is more neutral in energy.


<!-- chunk -->

### Has no toxic effects but is contraindicated with signs of heat, in acute

<!-- chunk -->

### diseases, high fevers, or inflammation


<!-- chunk -->

### Warming and moistening


<!-- chunk -->

### Adaptogen, hypertensive, immune stimulant, and tonic


<!-- chunk -->

### 2–4 ounces 2 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:4, 30% alcohol); 1–2 ml (0.2–0.4 tsp.) 1–3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:5); 1–3 ml (0.2–0.6 tsp.) 1–3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

# GOLDENSEAL

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Hydrastis canadensis

<!-- chunk -->

### Goldenseal is a locally acting antibiotic, meaning it has to come in contact with

<!-- chunk -->

### the infected tissue, and a mild immune stimulant, useful in urinary and digestive

<!-- chunk -->

### tract infections. It is very drying to the mucous membranes and particularly

<!-- chunk -->

### helpful after the acute infection has passed and there is lingering stagnation in

<!-- chunk -->

### the respiratory, digestive, or urinary mucous membranes. Goldenseal lowers

<!-- chunk -->

### blood sugar and, like most bitters, stimulates digestion. It is a specific remedy

<!-- chunk -->

### for diarrhea caused by giardia. It may be used as a wash for sore red eyes and as

<!-- chunk -->

### a topical application for canker sores.

<!-- chunk -->

### Goldenseal is overharvested, and other herbs should be used as substitutes

<!-- chunk -->

### when possible. Coptis root, Oregon grape, and barberry all contain the alkaloid

<!-- chunk -->

### berberine, and have similar antimicrobial properties as goldenseal.


<!-- chunk -->

### Goldenseal is safe when used at the recommended dosages and

<!-- chunk -->

### times, but should not be used as a single herb for longer than 2 weeks. It is

<!-- chunk -->

### contraindicated in dry conditions. When used for long periods, it can cause

<!-- chunk -->

### malabsorption of B vitamins, resulting in fatigue and listlessness. Goldenseal

<!-- chunk -->

### should be used under professional supervision during pregnancy.


<!-- chunk -->

### Alterative (blood purifier), antibacterial, antiseptic, and digestive

<!-- chunk -->

### tonic


<!-- chunk -->

### Felter: Relaxed mucous membranes, with feeble

<!-- chunk -->

### circulation, and profuse mucus flow of thick, tenacious, yellowish or greenish-

<!-- chunk -->

### yellow character. Gastric irritability and anorexia.


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:5, 60% alcohol); 10 drops to 2 ml (0.4 tsp.) 2–4 times


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried root (1:8); 2.5–10 ml (0.5–2 tsp.) 2–4 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### 500–2,000 mg, 2–3 times daily


<!-- chunk -->

### Use the dry powered herb as a snuff; works well with bayberry; can

<!-- chunk -->

### also be applied topically for skin ulcerations or used as an ingredient in

<!-- chunk -->

### poultices.

# HORSETAIL

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Equisetum arvense

<!-- chunk -->

### Horsetail is rich in the mineral silica, which is used along with calcium to form

<!-- chunk -->

### bones, nails, hair, and skin. Silica adds elasticity to tissues, making them strong

<!-- chunk -->

### but not brittle. It is astringent and is useful for internal bleeding, such as blood in

<!-- chunk -->

### the urine. It has a mild diuretic effect.


<!-- chunk -->

### Excessive consumption may lead to a thiamine deficiency. The

<!-- chunk -->

### powdered herb is not recommended for children, but the tea is okay.


<!-- chunk -->

### Diuretic, hemostatic, kidney tonic, mineralizer, and vulnerary


<!-- chunk -->

### Rolla Thomas: A mild diuretic, invaluable in gravel and

<!-- chunk -->

### irritation of the urinary organs, with dysuria and pain after urinating; also in

<!-- chunk -->

### suppression of urine and dropsical affections.


<!-- chunk -->

### Dried herb (1:5, 35% alcohol); 1–2 ml (0.2–0.4 tsp.) 3 times daily

# KAVA-KAVA

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

# LICORICE

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Glycyrrhiza glabra

<!-- chunk -->

### Licorice is a strong mucosal anti-inflammatory that can be used for gastric,

<!-- chunk -->

### esophageal, urinary, and respiratory inflammation. It eases dry coughs and sore

<!-- chunk -->

### throats when used as a tea or syrup. Licorice root helps to stabilize blood sugar

<!-- chunk -->

### levels and is useful in treating both hypoglycemia and diabetes. It is used in

<!-- chunk -->

### many traditional Chinese medicine formulations as a small part of the formula.


<!-- chunk -->

### Although licorice is a safe herb, some cautions are necessary when

<!-- chunk -->

### taking large doses for long periods of time. Licorice should be avoided in cases

<!-- chunk -->

### of high blood pressure or when taking digitalis. It causes retention of water and

<!-- chunk -->

### sodium and excretion of potassium, which can cause edema (water retention),

<!-- chunk -->

### high blood pressure, heart palpitations, or a slowing of the heartbeat. Vertigo

<!-- chunk -->

### (dizziness) and headaches are early symptoms of overuse of licorice.

<!-- chunk -->

### Taking a potassium supplement with licorice can help counteract some of

<!-- chunk -->

### these effects. These side effects are much more likely to occur when using

<!-- chunk -->

### licorice extracts or licorice-derived drugs than when taking whole licorice root.

<!-- chunk -->

### Deglycyrrhizinated licorice (DGL) is free of adverse effects. Use in pregnancy

<!-- chunk -->

### only under the supervision of a qualified herbalist or practitioner. Small

<!-- chunk -->

### quantities as part of a formula are okay during pregnancy.


<!-- chunk -->

### Adaptogen, anti-inflammatory, antitussive, demulcent (mucilant),

<!-- chunk -->

### and hypertensive

# LILY OF THE VALLEY

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Convallaria majalis

<!-- chunk -->

### Lily of the valley contains cardiac glycosides that affect the heart like digitalis

<!-- chunk -->

### but are less toxic. Lily of the valley normalizes heart action and increases blood

<!-- chunk -->

### pressure in hypotensive people. The crushed leaves of the fresh plant can be

<!-- chunk -->

### applied topically for drawing out infection and slivers.


<!-- chunk -->

### This toxic botanical is for professional use only. A toxic dose may

<!-- chunk -->

### cause nausea, vomiting, cardiac arrhythmias, hypertension, restlessness,

<!-- chunk -->

### trembling, confusion, weakness, depression, circulatory collapse, and death. Use

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

# LOBELIA

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Lobelia inflata

<!-- chunk -->

### Lobelia is a powerful antispasmodic herb. It dilates the bronchial passages to

<!-- chunk -->

### ease asthma attacks and eases pain caused by tension. It helps to clear lymphatic

<!-- chunk -->

### congestion and can be applied topically to insect bites and stings.


<!-- chunk -->

### The FDA considers lobelia to be poisonous, and many sources claim

<!-- chunk -->

### it will cause convulsions, coma, and death. These are potential effects of its

<!-- chunk -->

### principal alkaloid lobeline, but there is no record of the whole herb causing these

<!-- chunk -->

### problems in anyone. Lobelia is an emetic and makes you throw up if you take

<!-- chunk -->

### too much. Lobelia can produce severe symptoms (nausea, profuse sweating,

<!-- chunk -->

### vomiting, and deep relaxation), but these symptoms typically pass quickly and

<!-- chunk -->

### the person feels better afterward. However, because of these effects, lobelia is

<!-- chunk -->

### not recommended for weak, debilitated persons or persons who are deeply

<!-- chunk -->

### relaxed. Lobelia is not recommended for long-term use and should be used

<!-- chunk -->

### cautiously during pregnancy. To avoid unpleasant effects such as nausea and

<!-- chunk -->

### vomiting, use small, repeated doses instead of large, infrequent doses, or use it as

<!-- chunk -->

### part of a formula.


<!-- chunk -->

### Relaxing, slightly warming, and slightly drying


<!-- chunk -->

### Acrid, anti-arrhythmic, antispasmodic, antitussive, bronchial

<!-- chunk -->

### dilator, emetic, expectorant, hypotensive, nervine, and vasodilator


<!-- chunk -->

### Rolla Thomas: Sense of fullness and oppression in

<!-- chunk -->

### precordial region; oppression of chest and difficult respiration; sharp, lancinating

<!-- chunk -->

### pain starting in heart and radiating to left shoulder and arm; mucus rattling in

<!-- chunk -->

### throat; full, oppressed pulse, weak pulse—stimulant doses, 10–20 drops at a

<!-- chunk -->

### single dose in angina pectoris; 10 drops in 4 ounces water in ordinary disease;

<!-- chunk -->

### combined with lavender for asthenic bronchitis of the child.

# MEADOWSWEET

<!-- chunk -->

## Latin name: Filipendula ulmaria

<!-- chunk -->

### Meadowsweet contains salicin, a compound similar to aspirin, but without the

<!-- chunk -->

### negative side effects. It’s useful for reducing pain and inflammation, but it takes

<!-- chunk -->

### 6–8 hours to start acting. It settles the stomach and acts as a natural antacid. It

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->

### Because of its salicin content, some herbalists think meadowsweet

<!-- chunk -->

<!-- chunk -->
